   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Philippine languages
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>

          <img alt="{{{mapalt}}}" data-file-height="484" data-file-width="729" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Philippine_languages_map.svg/300px-Philippine_languages_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Philippine_languages_map.svg/450px-Philippine_languages_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Philippine_languages_map.svg/600px-Philippine_languages_map.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>

         <div style="text-align:left;">
          The Philippine languages, per Adelaar and Himmelmann (2005)
         </div>
        </td>

      <p>
       In linguistics, the
       <b>
        Philippine languages
       </b>
       are a proposal by Zorc (1986) and
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Blust" title="Robert Blust">
        Robert Blust
       </a>
       (1991) that all the languages of the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </a>
       and northern
       <a href="/wiki/Sulawesi" title="Sulawesi">
        Sulawesi
       </a>
       —except
       <a href="/wiki/Sama%E2%80%93Bajaw_languages" title="Sama–Bajaw languages">
        Sama–Bajaw
       </a>
       (languages of the "Sea Gypsies") and a few languages of
       <a href="/wiki/Palawan" title="Palawan">
        Palawan
       </a>
       —form a
       <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">
        subfamily
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">
        Austronesian languages
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although the Philippines is near the center of
       <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">
        Austronesian
       </a>
       expansion from
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Taiwan" title="Geography of Taiwan">
        Formosa
       </a>
       , there is little linguistic diversity among the approximately 150 Philippine languages, suggesting that earlier diversity has been erased by the spread of the ancestor of the modern Philippine languages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">
        Classification
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Philippine_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Classification">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       From approximately north to south, the Philippine languages are divided into the following subgroups:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Batanic_languages" title="Batanic languages">
         Batanic languages
        </a>
        (4 languages between
        <a href="/wiki/Batanes" title="Batanes">
         Batanes
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">
         Formosa
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Northern_Luzon_languages" title="Northern Luzon languages">
         Northern Luzon languages
        </a>
        (40 languages, including
        <a href="/wiki/Ilocano_language" title="Ilocano language">
         Ilocano
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Pangasinan_language" title="Pangasinan language">
         Pangasinan
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Central_Luzon_languages" title="Central Luzon languages">
         Central Luzon languages
        </a>
        (5 languages, including
        <a href="/wiki/Sambalic_languages" title="Sambalic languages">
         Sambal
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Kapampangan_language" title="Kapampangan language">
         Kapampangan
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mindoro_languages" title="Northern Mindoro languages">
         Northern Mindoro languages
        </a>
        (or North Mangyan; 3 languages)
       </li>
       <li>
        <span id="Greater_Central_Philippine_languages">
         Greater Central Philippine languages
        </span>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Southern_Mindoro_languages" title="Southern Mindoro languages">
           Southern Mindoro languages
          </a>
          (or South Mangyan; 3 languages)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Central_Philippine_languages" title="Central Philippine languages">
           Central Philippine languages
          </a>
          (40 languages, including
          <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">
           Tagalog
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Bikol_languages" title="Bikol languages">
           Bikol languages
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Visayan_languages" title="Visayan languages">
           Visayan languages
          </a>
          )
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Palawan_languages" title="Palawan languages">
           Palawan languages
          </a>
          (3 languages)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Subanon_language" title="Subanon language">
           Subanen languages
          </a>
          (6 languages)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Danao_languages" title="Danao languages">
           Danao languages
          </a>
          (3 languages, including
          <a href="/wiki/Maguindanao_language" title="Maguindanao language">
           Maguindanao
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Maranao_language" title="Maranao language">
           Maranao
          </a>
          )
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Manobo_languages" title="Manobo languages">
           Manobo languages
          </a>
          (15 languages)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Gorontalo%E2%80%93Mongondow_languages" title="Gorontalo–Mongondow languages">
           Gorontalo–Mongondow languages
          </a>
          (9 languages of
          <a href="/wiki/Gorontalo" title="Gorontalo">
           Gorontalo
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/North_Sulawesi" title="North Sulawesi">
           North Sulawesi
          </a>
          )
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kalamian_languages" title="Kalamian languages">
         Kalamian languages
        </a>
        (2 languages of northern
        <a href="/wiki/Palawan" title="Palawan">
         Palawan
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/South_Mindanao_languages" title="South Mindanao languages">
         South Mindanao languages
        </a>
        (5 languages)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Sangiric_languages" title="Sangiric languages">
         Sangiric languages
        </a>
        (4 languages of
        <a href="/wiki/Sangihe_Islands" title="Sangihe Islands">
         Sangir
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Talaud_Islands" title="Talaud Islands">
         Talaud Islands
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Minahasan_languages" title="Minahasan languages">
         Minahasan languages
        </a>
        (5 languages of
        <a href="/wiki/North_Sulawesi" title="North Sulawesi">
         North Sulawesi
        </a>
        )
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In addition, the
       <a href="/wiki/Ati_language" title="Ati language">
        Ati
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Umiray_Dumaget_language" title="Umiray Dumaget language">
        Umiray Dumaget
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Manide_language" title="Manide language">
        Manide
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Inagta_Alabat_language" title="Inagta Alabat language">
        Inagta Alabat languages
       </a>
       are unclassified within the Philippine family.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary_comparison">
        Vocabulary comparison
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Philippine_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Vocabulary comparison">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Comparison chart between several selected Philippine languages spoken from north to south with
       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Austronesian_language" title="Proto-Austronesian language">
        Proto-Austronesian
       </a>

        : Vol. 85: Iss. 1, Article 15.
       </li>
      </ul>
